**PREFACE.**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724738424Screenshot2024-08-27112949.png"/>

 THE present edition of the *Bháminívilása* is based on the following six copies :—

* A.*— A MS. from the library of the late Aṇṇa Shastri Agashe of Ratnagiri, lent to me by Mr. Janardan Balaji Modak, B.A. It consists of 30 oblong leaves legibly and correctly written. It bears no date.

* B*.— The Paris edition of the poem by M. A. Bergaigne, published in 1872. This edition is a scholarly attempt, and gives a tolerably correct text.

* C*.—The Calcutta print of 1872 by Professor Táránáth.

* D.*—A MS. of the poem deposited at the Bombay Branch of the Royal Asiatic Society's Library, Bombay. It is one of a series of MSS. bound together in one volume, consists of 12 oblong leaves, and bears date *Aśvina śukla 10th*, giving no year. The colophon at the end of the MS. runs thus :—

** इति श्रीमदखिलान्ध्रवेङ्गिनारिकुलावतंसु *(sic)* पण्डितराजजगन्नाथनिर्मिते भामिनीविलासे शान्तश्चतुर्थो विलासः समाप्तः॥**

* E.*— A MS. from the Government Collection, Deccan College, Poona, kindly lent by Dr. R. G. Bhandarkar. It contains 114 oblong leaves, and is accompanied by a commentary of no great merit. It bears date 1846 *Saṁvat*, the colophon at the end being—

** इति श्रीमदखिलान्ध्रवेङ्गिकुलावतं *(sic)* पण्डितराजजगन्नाथनिर्मिते भामिनीविलासे शान्तश्चतुर्थो विलासः समाप्तः॥ सं १८४६।**

** ***F.*—A MS. belonging to myself. It is a faithful copy of a MS. in the possession of my friend and teacher, the late Mr. Vishņu Krishna Chipluṇkar.

 In addition to these copies I have very often consulted the readings given in the *Rasagangádhara.*

* *All these copies have been carefully collated for this edition. One point in regard to them, which requires special notice, is the unusual diversity respecting the number of stanzas contained in each. The following table will show at a glance how they stand in this respect to each other, and to the present edition:—



| | | | | | |
|:-------------:|:-----:|:------:|:-------:|:------:|:------:|
| Copy. | V. I. | V. II. | V. III. | V. IV. | TOTAL. |
| A........... | 126 | 184 | 19 | 46 | 375 |
| B........... | 127 | 182 | 19 | 46 | 374 |
| C........... | 126 | 102 | 18 | 46 | 292 |
| D........... | 130 | 183 | 19 | 32 | 361 |
| E........... | 100 | 102 | 19 | 31 | 252 |
| F........... | 101 | 101 | 19 | 32 | 253 |
| Present Ed... | 129 | 183 | 19 | 45 | 376 |

 The *Bháminīvilása* is, like the three *śatakas* of Bhartrihari, a compilation of miscellaneous stanzas. It has no plot, no context. Each stanza has an occasion of its own, and is complete in itself. In this, no doubt, is to he found the cause of the diversity above noticed. In such compilations, there is ample opportunity for dropping or interpolating whole stanzas without the least fear of detection; for the guiding principle of context being absent, it is very difficult, sometimes impossible, to ascertain whether a particular portion of them is genuine or spurious. In the case of the present poem a careful examination of all the works of the author would, perhaps, make such a task possible; but sufficient materials for such an examination are not at hand, at present at least. Under these circumstances I have thought it advisable to give insertion in the text, with two exceptions, to all such stanzas as were to be found in at least two of the copies consulted. Following this principle I have relegated to the appendix three stanzas from the first *vilása* which are found only in D. On the same principle I have admitted into the text 6 *ślokas*, two of which (I. 128, IV. 42) are common to this poem with the *Pránábharaṇa* and four (IV. 1, 10, 11, 14) with the *Karuṇálahari*. I have followed this procedure, because it is yet doubtful to which of the poems the stanzas in question. really belong. One of the two stanzas (I. 128) which occur also in *Práṇábharaṇa,* appears to have been interpolated in that poem. It takes its place there after what should naturally be the concluding stanza of the poem, and also after Jagannátha has apparently concluded his own exegesis on it. The four stanzas, again, which occur in the *Karuṇálahari,* are found only in some copies of that poem. The two exceptions noted above are the stanzas marked II. 113, IV. 13 in the Appendix. I have given my reasons there for not admitting them into the text. I am fully conscious that, in following my principle, I may have incorporated in the text some stanzas which, on further inquiry, may prove not to belong to it. I myself have pointed out elsewhere that II. 120, 142 do not appear to deserve a place in the *Sṛingáravilása* where they occur. In the absence of any authority, however, I have thought it better to retain such stanzas in the text, on the consideration that all of them are found in the *Rasagangádhara* as Jagannatha's own, and that, in a work like the present, they cannot disturb the continuity of the poem. However, whenever a stanza is omitted by any of the copies collated, I have taken care invariably to mark, the omission in foot-notes. The order of *ṣlokas* is not always the same in all the copies, and, in cases of divergence, I have had to be guided by the arrangement of the majority of them. As to *variæ lectiones*, happily they are few, and are mostly too unimportant to deserve notice. I have adopted, generally, the reading of the majority of the copies, and, in a few cases, where such a course appeared necessary, the one that I thought best. But have not considered it worth while to notice the variants, except in some special cases. It should be remembered in this connection that Jagann*á*tha himself often twists his verses, in a variety of ways, in the *Rasagangádhara*, to meet the exigencies of Alankára, and it is sometimes difficult to determine the version which he subsequently adopted in the *Bháminívilása.*

 The Sanskrit gloss which accompanies the text is intended for the ordinary reader as well as for the more advanced student. It does not profess to be a full commentary dealing with each word of the stanza according to its place in syntactical construction. It explains the connection of words, wherever that is obscure, and gives the meanings of hard words and unusual phrases, the side-meanings of words and sentences, and the bearing of the whole stanza, when necessary. These things, it is hoped, will be useful to the ordinary reader. Further, it solves, in some cases, difficulties of grammar, often explains the *alankáras* and *rasas,* and points out the beauties of the stanza according to the way of native critics. This information, I am afraid, will be rather beyond the comprehension of the general reader, but I persuade myself that it will be acceptable to the University student and to others who wish to make a critical study of the poem. In writing the gloss reliance has principally been placed on the *Rasagangádhara* which is the best, and practically the author's own commentary on the present work, though Nágeśabhaṭṭa's gloss on the *Rasagangádhara*, as far as it is published, Professor Táránáth's annotations and the commentary which accompanies E have not unfrequently been consulted. I have often had occasion to reject Professor Táránáth's explanations, and, in a place or two, I have taken the liberty, though with great diffidence, to differ from the learned glossarist of the *Rasagangádhara* also. I have borrowed whole sentences from the *Rasagangádhara*, wherever they appeared suitable for my purposes, and have occasionally selected some words and phrases from the other sources also. On my part I have spared no pains to makethe gloss as useful as I could.

How far I have succeeded, I must leave it to the reader to judge.

 The introduction is principally based on information yielded by an examination of those of Jagannátha's works to which I had access. Some of his works, which are known to me by name, have not been available for inspection. Owing, thus, to the incomplete nature of the materials at my command, it has not been so full and exhaustive as I could wish; but I did not think it advisable to wait for more materials as that would have indefinitely delayed the publication of the book. Of course, if I succeed in discovering further sources of information I shall be very glad to retouch my account of the poet.

 There is one more point which requires a little explanation. In this edition I have invariably used the *anusvára* sign in those places where usually its corresponding nasal is substituted. This *anusvára* system is followed in our old MSS., and is, withal, very convenient in printing. Indeed, I see no reason why it should not come into more general use.

 It remains for me, in concluding, to offer my hearty thanks to my learned teacher, Mahámahopádhyáya Rajaram Shastri Bodas, of Elphinstone College, who has rendered me valuable assistance in the preparation of this edition.

**L. R. VAIDYA.**

*September* 30*th,* 1887.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724749001Screenshot2024-08-27112949.png"/>

**INTRODUCTION.**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724763664Screenshot2024-08-27112949.png"/>

*I. Tradition about Jagannátha; II. Its validity examined; III. His date; IV. His personal history; V. His works; VI. Other authors of the same name; VII. Jagannátha as an author; VIII. Conclusion.*

 I. In the general absence of any land-marks in the history of Sanskrit authors, it is a relief to possess means, though as yet imperfect, of ascertaining with certainty the date of Jagannátha Paṇḍit, the author of the *Bháminívilása*, and of gleaning some bits of authentic information about his personal history. In India tradition springs up and obtains credit and currency with such rapidity and ease, that it soon gets inextricably intermingled with history, and often baffles all attempts at honest differentiation. Even in the case of so modern an author as Jagannátha, it has got such a strong hold on the mind of the people that his personal history is now lost in a shroud of popular stories, more or less improbable. Indeed, a close acquaintance with the poet's works ought to dispel the mist to some extent. Jagannátha, however, is one of those authors who enjoy a high reputation among Paṇḍits, but whose works are unfortunately little known and less read. It may be remarked, moreover, that Paṇḍits of the old type do not like to be disturbed in their fond beliefs and happy illusions. Various anecdotes about our author, in a variety of versions, have thus obtained very wide currency. Apart from their truth or otherwise, they are very interesting, and, before we proceed to state what may be known of the poet, we propose to give here, in the most sensible version current, as many of them as are known to us.

 1. Not finding favour with the princes of the Carnatic, it is said that Jagannátha went to Northern India, there to build a name and a fortune for himself. At Jeypore he worsted many Pandits in controversy, and established a new school for the study of the Sástras. About this time, a learned Kází from the Court of Delhi travelled over India, holding religious discussions wherever he went, defeating learned Paṇḍits and establishing that the faith of Islam was the only true faith on the face of the earth. When Jagannátha heard of these religious disputations and of the mortification that many Hindu scholars were put to, he zealously studied Persian for one year, made himself thoroughly acquainted with the tenets of Islamism, and entered lists with the Kází. The Kází's controversial weapons were blunt before Jagannátha's powerful polemics, which enabled him to win a decisive victory, and to prove to the Emperor's satisfaction that, it was, at best, prudent for born Islamites to adhere to their own faith, but that Islamism presented no feature which could attract followers from other creeds. The Emperor was highly pleased with Jagannátha's extraordinary abilities and attached him to the Imperial Court.

 2. Emperor Akbar, to whose time tradition assigns Jagannátha, had a very lovely daughter of the name of Lavangí by a Rajput wife. In the fulness of youth, endowed with all perfections that nature could bestow, she one day heard that there was, in her father's court, a young Pandit of exceptional abilities and personal attractions of the name of Jagannátha, and watched for an opportunity to have a sight of him. The desired opportunity came and left Lavangí completely disconsolate and determined either to marry Jagannátha or not to marry at all. One day, while Akbar and Jagannátha were playing at chess, the former felt thirsty and ordered water. Thereupon, with a small water-jar on her head, Lavangí came into the presence of the Emperor, who, being then in high spirits, asked Jagannátha to describe her in that posture. The poet at once sang :— "This pretty-breasted lady, with a pitcher on her head, apparelled in nice scarlet garments, looks as if she snatches the mind of the whole world and carries it away in her pitcher" *(a)*. This ready wit so much delighted the Emperor, that he expressed his readiness to grant any request of Jagannátha Paṇḍit. The Paṇḍit again sings:— "I beg not elephants; I ask not for horses; my mind has never been in riches; may this pretty- breasted deer-eyed Lavangi bestow her favours on me. Should the butter-soft *yavanī* ever grace my bed, to this earth I would give the palm; not the garden of Indra would afford me pleasure" *(b)*. This unexpected request took the Emperor by surprise mingled with regret. But unable to break his word, he put it as a condition, precedent to the fulfilment of his promise, that Jagannátha should mess with him. Even to this condition, which involved loss of caste, the Paṇḍit agreed in order to secure the object of his love.

 3. While Jagannátha was basking in the sunshine of Royalty's favour at Delhi, he got an invitation from some other prince to partake of the hospitality and patronage of his court. To this call the poet sent the following spirited reply :—

 "Either the Lord of Delhi or the Lord of the Universe alone can grant my desires; gifts from other princes (at

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724753831Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

***(a).* इयं सुस्तनी मस्तकन्यस्तकुम्भा  
 कुसुम्भारुणं चारु चेलं वसाना।  
 समस्तस्य लोकस्य चेतःप्रवृत्तिं  
 गृहीत्वा घटे न्यस्य यातीव भाति॥  
*(b)*. न याचे गजालिं न वा वाजिराजिं  
 न वित्तेषु चित्तं मदीयं कदाचित्।  
 इयं सुस्तनी मस्तकन्यस्तकुम्भा  
 लवङ्गी कुरङ्गीदृगङ्गीकरोतु ॥  
   यवनी नवनीतकोमलाङ्गी  
 शयनीये यदि लभ्यते कदाचित्।  
 अवनीतलमेव साधु मन्ये  
 न वनी माघवनी विलासहेतुः॥ **

best) may suffice for vegetable dishes: may suffice for condiments" *(c)*.

 4. It is said that Jagannátha propitiated, by means of hard penance, a certain goddess who conferred on him the following boon:—

 "Travel all over the Kurus and do not be doubtful of success in controversies with your adversaries; accept of me one boon, dear son, and explain the Ṣástras" *(d).*

 5. Haradíkshita, the teacher of the celebrated modern grammarian, Nágeśabhaṭṭa, once went to Delhi in the hope of getting some reward from the Emperor. Before presenting himself to Majesty, he called on Panditarája, and expressed a desire to hold with him a discussion on grammar at the court. Paṇḍitarája consented and asked him to visit the court the next day. But fully conscious of the great abilities of Haradíkshita, he armed himself with a charmed amulet, and embraced the visitor as he entered the court. A sort of dulness came upon Haradíkshita; he began to make ludicrous blunders at the very outset of the discussion, and had at last to leave the court, covered with disgrace. On returning home he himself could not account for his silly and senseless replies. Keen, indeed, is the distress of defeat, and to Haradíkshita it was keener than death. In his disappointment he resolved to destroy himself if he did not succeed that night in securing the means of vanquishing Jagannátha. Through the favour of a divinity the requisite means were obtained, and, on the following day, the tables being turned, Haradíkshita came off successful.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724754801Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

***(c)* दिल्लीश्वरो वा जगदीश्वरो वा  
 मनोरथान् पूरयितुं समर्थः।  
 अन्यैर्नृपालैः परिदीयमानं  
 शाकाय वा स्याल्लवणाय वा स्यात्॥**

***(d)* आकुरुदेशं विचरेर्मा कुरु परवादिनिर्जये शङ्काम्।  
 स्वीकुरु वरमेकं मे व्याकुरुभो वत्स शास्त्राणि॥**

 6. When Paṇḍitarája had passed his best years in happiness at the court of Delhi with his *yavana* wife, he repented of his conduct and went to Banaras with the intention of passing the remainder of his life there. The great *Śrotriya* Appadíkshita, while in the holy city on a pilgrimage, went one afternoon to pay a visit to Jagannátha Paṇḍit. To his great surprise he found Paṇḍitarája lying on a couch with his *Yavaní* at that improper hour, and, pretending to be ignorant who it was, said :—

 "How can you sleep fearless in this decline of life, when death knocks at the door? ”

 Hearing these words, Jagannátha got down to receive the *Śrotriya*, when the latter proceeded :—

 "Or, free from anxiety, you may sleep; for near you stands awake the mother Ganges" *(e).*  
 7. The learned Bráhmans of Banaras were anxious to overlook Jagannátha's past delinquencies and to admit him into the caste. But he would not consent to any proposal which would separate him from his beloved *Yavaní.* When he saw that he could not expect any clemency from the Bráhmans of Banaras on his own terms, he one day sat with his *Yavaní* on the topmost step of one of the *ghats* of the Ganges and began to sing the praises of the sacred stream in charming strains. The stream swelled and rose one step higher as each successive stanza was sung. The *ghat* had fifty-two steps, and, at the conclusion of the fifty-second stanza, the sacred waters touched Jagannátha and his *Yavaní* and washed away their sin. It is said that they threw themselves into the river and were never seen again. This hymn of fifty-two *ślokas* to the Ganges is now known as Gangálahari among the people, and is read all over India.

 II. Such are the anecdotes about Jagannátha commonly related by the people. Let us see how far they may be

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724764917Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

***(e)* See Bháminívilása, IV. 30.**

believed. As for the first story, we know from extraneous sources, and can infer from Jagannátha's surname as well as from the name of his father, that he was a native of Southern India. It is certain, as will be seen later on, that he passed many years of his life in Northern India; and it may also be true that he had a knowledge of the Persian tongue. There are extant, it is said, some *ślokas* by Paṇḍitarája, half Sanskrit and half Persian; and he is also reported to have translated into Sanskrit a Persian work on Astronomy. The anecdote does not mention the name of the Emperor who extended his patronage to Jagannátha, but we know that more than one of the Mughal Emperors were great patrons of Sanskrit letters. So far as we are yet aware, there is nothing in the poet's works that either confirms or contradicts the story, which, by itself, is not quite unworthy of belief.

 The second story is specifically referred to Emperor Akbar; but, as we hope to show further on, Jagannátha did not flourish in that Emperor's reign and was not connected with his Court. The *ślokas* given in the story are not found in any known work of Jagannátha, and there is no other authority for holding that they were his composition. History supplies us with no information about Lavangí; the *Ain-i-Akbari* descends into very minute particulars of Akbar's life; but it makes no reference whatever either to her or to Jagannatha. There is, moreover, one item in the story itself, which renders it very improbable. It is preposterous to think, especially when the strict *paḍadá* system of the Muhammadans is taken into consideration, that a princess should come into the presence of strangers with a water-jar on her head. We do not deny, however, that there may be some little foundation for the story, since it has got such a wide currency. Jagannátha may perhaps have lived with some *yavaní.*

* *The third anecdote is, of course, quite probable, though we cannot vouch for its truth.

 The fourth and fifth stories land us into regions where faith predominates over reason. They hardly call for any remark, though it may be observed in connection with the fifth story, that it seems hardly probable that Nágeśabhaṭṭa's teacher should have lived in Jagannátha's time(ƒ).

 As regards the sixth story, there is some ground for saying that Jagannátha passed the last days of his life in Banaras, though it would appear from the reading of several copies of *Bháminívilása*, that he fixed on Mathurá as his last residence*(g)*. It is also probable that the great Draviḍa writer was his rival and contemporary*(h)*; but whether the two authors ever met at Banaras under the circumstances mentioned is more than can be easily decided. The *áryá* itself occurs in *Bháminívilása* and also in *Rasagangádhara* as Jagannátha's own*(i),* whereas, according to the anecdote, its authorship would belong to Appadíkshita.

 The last story, again, travels ground beyond the sphere of history. Indeed, the *Gangálahari* consists of fifty-two stanzas; and there are some *ślokas* in it which lend some colour to the story*(j).* But that proves nothing. Equally impassioned verses are found in other hymns, for instance, in the *Kekávali* of our Maháráshtra bard, Moropant. Probably

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724767960Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

 * (f)* Dr. Kielhorn states that "Nilkanṭh Shástri Thatte, when about 80 years old, was known to Anant Shástri, who was then quite a young man." As Anant Shástri Pendhárkar was 72 years old in 1868, he must have seen Nilkanṭh Shastri about 1825 A.C. Vaidyanáth Páyagunde, who studied directly under Nágeśabhaṭṭa was Nilkanṭh Shástri's teacher. If, then, we allow 25 years for each generation and calculate back from 1825 for three generations-those of V. Páyagunde, Nágeśabhaṭṭa and his teacher—we get 1750 A. C. as the approximate date of Haradíkshita, if that is really the name of Nágojí's teacher. (See Kielhorn's Edition of the *Paribhásheduśekhara*, Introduction, xxv.) The title of Nágojí's gloss on the *Rasagangádhara*(गुरुमर्मप्रकाश) at first sight suggests that Nágojí was perhaps Jagannátha's pupil. But the opening line of the gloss thus explains its purport :—

**नत्वा गङ्गाधरं मर्मप्रकाशं तनुते गुरुम्।**

* (g)* *See Bh*. IV. 44 and gloss.  
* (h)* See *infra*, page 21 (z).  
* (i) Bh.* IV. 30; *Rasagangádhara, Ákshepaprakaraṇa.*  
* (j)* See *Gangálahari* 6, 28, 30, 36, 37, 39, 46, and 47.

the existence of such verses, coupled with other circumstances in Jagannátha's life, may have given rise to this popular belief. Besides, if the story means that the *Gangálahari* was the poet's last production, and that immediately after he threw himself into the Ganges, it may easily be shown to be false. Jagannátha has extracted many verses from this small poem in the *Rasagangádhara*, and has once alluded to it by name(*k*). This means, of course, that the poet lived after the composition of the *Gangálahari* to write his great treatise on *Alankára.*

 III. Tradition being thus disposed of, let us proceed to fix Jagannátha's date. That he was patronized by an Emperor of Delhi is amply proved by the extravagant panegyrics that he bestows on the Lord of Delhi in the *Rasagangádhara(l)*, as well as by his own statement to that effect at the close of the *Bháminívilása(m)*. But, as we have already intimated, we

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724851010Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

*** (k) See infra, page 13 (b).***

***(l)* सुराणामारामादिह झटिति झञ्झानिलहताः  
 पतेयुः शाखीन्द्रा यदि तदखिलो नन्दति जनः।  
 किमेभिर्वा कार्यं शिव शिव विवेकेन विकलै-  
 श्चिरं जीवन्नास्तामधिधरणि दिल्लीनरपतिः॥**

***R. G., Ā**kshepaprakaraṇ**a.***

** सृष्टः सृष्टिकृता पुरा किल परित्रातुं जगन्मण्डलं  
 त्वं चण्डातप निर्दयं दहसि यज्ज्वालाजटालैः करैः।  
 संरम्भारुणलोचनो रणभुवि प्रस्थातुकामोऽधुना  
 जानीमो भवता न हन्त विदितो दिल्लीधरावल्लभः॥**

***R. G. Aprastutapraś**aṇsà.***

** माहात्म्यस्य परोवधिर्निजगृहं गम्भीरतायाः पिता  
 रत्नानामहमेक एव भुवने को वाऽपरो मादृशः।  
 इत्येवं परिचिन्त्य मास्म सहसा गर्वान्धकारं गमो  
 दुग्धाब्धे भवता समो विजयते दिल्लीधरावल्लभः ॥**

***R. G., Pratípaprakaraṇa.***

** अनुकूलभावमथवा पराङ्मुखत्वं सहैव नरलोके।  
 अन्योन्यविहितमन्त्रौ विधिदिल्लीवल्लभौ वहतः॥**

***R. G., Sahoktiprakara******ṇ******a.***

*(**m*****) *Bh*. IV. 44.**

reject, as unworthy of belief, the tradition which makes Jagannátha the Poet Laureate of Akbar and thus assigns him to the second half of the sixteenth century. On the one hand, there is complete absence of any allusion to Emperor Akbar in the known works of the author; and on the other, the several Muhammadan records of Akbar's reign make no reference whatever to Jagannátha. To add to this negative testimony, which, singly, can have no great probative force, we have Jagannátha's own statement that the title of Paṇḍitarája was bestowed on him by Emperor Sháh Jahán *(n),* his mention of the names of Jahángír and Sháh Jahán in the *Rasagangádhara (o),* and a short poem from his pen, eulogistic of Sháh Jahán's eldest and most favourite son, Dárá Shukoh *(p)*. Finally we find, as concurrent testimony, a statement in

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724851805Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

 *(n)* मूर्तिमतेव **नवाबासफखान**मनःप्रसादेन द्विजकुलसेवाहेवाकिवाङ्मनः कायेन माथुरकुलसमुद्रेन्दुना **रायमुकुन्दे**नादिष्टेन सार्वभौमश्री**शहाजहां**प्रसादाधिगतपण्डितराजपदवीविराजितेन **तैलङ्ग**कुलावतंसेन **पण्डितजगन्नाथेना**सफविलासाख्येयमाख्यायिका निरमीयत।

*Āsaphavilása, Introduction.*

(*०*) श्यामं यज्ञोपवीतं तव किमिति मषीसङ्गमात्कुत्र जातः  
सोऽयं शीतांशुकन्यापयसि कथमभूत्तज्जलं कज्जलाक्तम्।  
व्याकुप्य**न्नूरदीन**क्षितिरमणरिपुक्षोणिभृत्पक्ष्मलाक्षी-  
लक्षाक्षीणाश्रुधारासमुदितसरितां सर्वतः सङ्गमेन॥

*Uttaraprakaraṇa.*

भूमीनाथ शहाबुदीन भवतस्तुल्यो गुणानां गणै-  
रेतद्भूतभवप्रपञ्चविषये नास्तीति किं ब्रूमहे।  
धात नूतनकारणैर्यदि पुनः सृष्टिं नवां भावये-  
न्न स्यादेव तथापि तावकतुलालेशं दधानो नरः॥

*Asamaprakaraṇa.*

 "Núruddín Muhammad Jahángír and "Shihábuddín Muhammad Sháh Jahán" I were respectively the full names of Jahángír and Sháh Jahán. (See, *inter alia*, Blochmann's translation of *Ain-i-Akbari :* geneological tree at the end of Vol. I.)

*(p) Jagadábharaṇa.*

Muhammadan authors to the effect that Jagannátha got the title of *Kavirája* from Emperor Sháh Jahán *(q).*

 Now it is impossible to suppose that Jagannátha's career must have extended over three long reigns—those of Akbar, Jahángír and Sháh Jahán—embracing a period of full one hundred years (1556-1658). We know for certain that Jagannátha was chiefly patronized by Sháh Jahán. If so, the chronological distance between Sháh Jahán and Akbar renders it impossible that he should have been patronized by the latter also. As he writes a stanza in eulogy of Jahángír, he may have, perhaps, seen the latter end of that Emperor's reign; and as he has panegyrized Sháh Jahán's son Dárá Shukoh, it is possible that he may have witnessed the events of 1658*(r)*. This, at all events, appears certain that Jagannátha's active career lay between 1620 and 1660 A.C.

  IV. Jagannátha was born of the Tailanga family. His father's name was either Peramabhaṭṭa or Perubhaṭṭa and his mother's name Lakshmí(s). His father was a learned

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724853969Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

* * *(q)* "During Sháh Jahán's reign we find Jagnát'h, who received from Sháh Jahán the title of *Kabrái;* Dirang Khán; and Lál Khán, who got the title of *Gunasamundar* (ocean of excellence). Lál Khán was son-in-law to Bilás, son of Tánsen. Jagnát'h and Dirang Khán were both weighed in silver and received each 4,500 Rupees."

 Blochmann's translation of *Ain-i-Akbari,* Vol. I., p. 613, note.  
* Jagnát'h-*Jagannátha; *Kabrái-Kavirája; Gunsamundar-Guṇasamudra.*

 *(r)* It is not, however, necessary to suppose either that Jagannátha must have seen Jahángír's reign or that he must have lived to witness the temporary ascension of Dárá to the throne of Delhi. It is quite within the range of probability that he must have written eulogies on Sháb Jahán's father and son to please his patron. We know, besides, that Dárá patronized Paṇḍits, while yet a prince. (See Sir H. Elliot's *History of India*, Vol. VII., p.179.)

**(*s)* तैलङ्गान्वयमङ्गलालयमहालक्ष्मीदयालालितः  
 श्रीमत्पेरमभट्टसूनुरनिशं विद्वल्ललाटन्तपः।  
 सन्तुष्टः कमताधिपस्य कवितामाकर्ण्य तद्वर्णनं  
 श्रीमत्पण्डितराजपण्डितजगन्नाथो व्यधासीदिदम्॥**

***Práṇábharaṇa*, 52.**

Paṇḍit and had mastered all the Śástras at Banaras under various teachers. He studied *Vedánta* under one Jnyánendrayati, the philosophical systems of Kaṇáda and Gautama under Mahendra, Jaimini's precepts (*Mimánsá)* under Khandadeva, and Patanjali's *Mahábháshya* under Víreśvara, surnamed Śesha*(t).* Jagannátha prosecuted his studies in the Sástras under his father*(u).* The best days of his life he passed in the North of India, at the Court of Delhi, under the patronage of Emperor Sháh Jahán, from whom he received the title of Paṇḍitaraja *(v)*. At the court he as well as one

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724854457Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

पाषाणादपि पीयूषं स्यन्दते यस्य ललिया।  
तं वन्दे **पेरु**\[दु\]भट्टाख्यं लक्ष्मीकान्तं महागुरुम्॥

*R.G., Introduction.*

 See also the passage from *Āsaphavilása* quoted above. I am told that पेरमभट्ट and पेरुभट्ट are two forms of the same name, the latter being a mere contraction of the former. In the colophons to D and E, Jagannátha's family-name is given as आन्ध्रर्वेगिनारि and आन्ध्रवेङ्गि respectively (see preface), and not as तैलङ्ग. Of course more reliance must be placed on what we believe to be the author's own statements.

*(t)* श्रीमज्ज्ञानेन्द्रभिक्षोरधिगतसकलब्रह्मविद्याप्रपञ्चः  
काणादीराक्षपादीरपि गहनगिरो यो महेन्द्रादवेदीत्।  
देवादेवाध्यगीष्ट स्मरहरनगरे शासनं जैमिनीयं  
शेषाङ्कप्राप्तशेषामलभणितिरभूत्सर्वविद्याधरो यः॥

*R. G., Introduction.*

  ...............'ज्ञानेन्द्राख्यपतेः सकाशादित्यर्थः ..............देवादेव। एवः प्रसिद्धौ। खण्डदेवादेवेत्यर्थः। ............. शेष इत्यङ्क उपनाम यस्य तस्माद्वीरेश्वरपण्डितात्प्राप्ता शेषस्य पतञ्जलेरमला भणितिर्महाभाष्यरूपा येन तादृशः।

Nágeśabhaṭṭa's gloss on the above.

 (*u*) See the stanza पाषाणादपि &c, quoted above. Perubhaṭṭa is there called महागुरु most probably in the double sense of father and teacher. Nágojí explains the महा that precedes गुरुम् by सर्वविद्यानामेकस्मादेव लाभात्तत्र महत्वम् I

* (v)* In addition to the passages quoted *supra, see Bh*. IV. 44. It is worthy of note, however, that the passage quoted from Blochmann's translation of the *Ain-i-Akbari* gives the title as *Kavirája* instead of *Paṇḍitarája.*

Dirang Khán was weighed in silver and received Rs. 4,500 *(w).* He was in some way connected with one Ráyamukunda of the Máthura family and also with a potentate of Kámarúpa of the name of Práṇanáráyaṇa*(x).* After a glorious career as an author and a controversialist he settled either in Mathurá or at Banaras, and passed his declining years there(*y).*

 To these bits principally gleaned from the author's works may be added, through the kindness of a friend, that Jagannátha was by caste a Tailanga Bráhman, probably a native of Rajamhendri district, and that one of his brother's descendants, named Lakshmídhararao, was translator of Southern languages to one of the Governors-General of India(*z).*

 V. Jagannátha incidentally states in the *Rasagangádhara* that he wrote five *laharis* or small hymns to several deities(*a)*. All of them are now recovered and published. They are:—

** Píyúshalahari—**more commonly known as *Gangálahari,* is a small but very beautiful hymn to the most sacred stream of India. It is mostly composed in the *Śikhariṇi* metre and consists of 52 stanzas. It has taken its place among the sacred writings of the people and is extensively read, though seldom with the critic's eye. As we have

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724855400Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

* (w)* See the passage quoted above from Blochmann's translation of the *Ain-i-Akbari.*

* (x)* See *Práṇábharaṇa* and the passage from *Āsaphavilasa quoted supra.*

* (y)* See *Bh. IV.* 44.

  (*z)* I owe this information to the kindness of my friend Mr. Babu Shastri Telang of Banaras. He has not supplied me with any authorities for his information, but I have reason to believe that it must be correct. I understand that Mr. Babu Shastri claims descent from Jagannátha Paṇḍit, and his surname is, no doubt, in favour of the claim.

 (*a*) **प्रबन्धस्य तु योगवासिष्ठरामायणे शान्तकरुणयो रत्नावल्यादीनि च शृङ्गारस्य व्यञ्जकत्वान्निदर्शनानि प्रसिद्धानि। मनिर्मिताश्च पञ्च लहर्यो भावस्य।**

***R. G., Anana I.***

already mentioned, the Rasagangádhara has many quotations from it, and in one place alludes to it by name *(b).*

** Sudhálahari**—is a short poem of 30 stanzas in the *Sragdhará* metre devoted to the celebration of the Glories of the Sun. It is apparently composed on the model of Mayúra's *Súryaśataka*, which is written in the same metre and praises the same deity. The descriptions in the poem are majestic in themselves, and the sonorous stanza adds to the majesty. Some stanzas from it are excerpted in the *Rasagangádhara* for purposes of illustration *(c)*.

** Amṛitalahari**— is a very short hymn to the Yamuná on the model of *Ś*ankaráchárya's celebrated hymn to the Ganges. It consists of 10 stanzas.

 **Karuṇálahari**—is a poem of about sixty stanzas, in which the poet dwells on his worldly miseries and seeks protection from Vishṇu. It is, in some copies, intituled *Vishṇulahari*, but the poet himself refers to it by the other name *(d).* Quotations from it occur in the *Rasagangádhara* *(e).*

 **Lakshmílahari**—is a short poem consisting of 41 *Śikhari*ṇ*i* stanzas. It extols Lakshmí, Vishṇu's consort. One stanza from it is quoted in the *Rasagangádhara,* and the same occurs in the *Bháminívilása* in a modified form (ƒ).

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724863175Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

***(b) *उदाहरणममृतलहर्याख्ये मदीये गङ्गास्तवे —  
    कृतक्षुद्राघौघानथ सपदि सन्तप्तमनसः  
    समुद्धर्तुं सन्ति त्रिभुवनतले तीर्थनिवहाः।  
    अपि प्रायश्चित्तप्रसरणपथातीतचरितान्  
    नरानूरीकर्तुं त्वमिव जननि त्वं विजयसे॥**

*R. G., Ananvayaprakaraṇa.*

 The title of the poem, as given in its last verse, is *Píyúshalahari,* not *Amṛitalahari* as given in the present passage. Considering that *Amṛitalahari* is the title of another of Jagannatha's poems, the name given here appears to be due to an oversight on the part of the poet.

(*c)* *Sudhálahari,* 1, 5, 6 and 24.  
* (d)* See Appendix.  
* (e)* *Karuṇálahari,* 3, 16, 25 and 55.  
* (f)* See *Bh.* II. 137.

** ** **Yamunávaraṇanachampú**—this work, which appears to be written partly in verse and partly in prose, is not available to me for inspection. It is mentioned as written by Jagannátha in the recent monthly publication, *Kávyamálá.* Two prose passages from a *Yamunávarṇana* are quoted in the *Rasagangádhara*, and it is probable that they were taken from this *Yamunávarṇanachampú (g).*

 The **Rasagangádhara**—is by far the most voluminous and important of our author's works. It is a treatise on poetics, written in masterly style, with great ability, sound reasoning, and consummate judgment, after a careful study of the previous works on the subject. Indeed, it may be said that Jagannátha has done for poetics what Bhaṭṭojídíkshita and Nágojíbhaṭṭa after him did for grammar. In this work the author discusses every disputed point at great length, fully examines the opinions of previous writers on it, and generally arrives at a satisfactory solution *(h).*

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725035657Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

* (g)* यत्र व्यङ्ग्यचमत्कारासमानाधिकरणो वाच्यचमत्कारस्तत्तृतीयम्। यथा यमुनावर्णनेः— ‘तनयमैनाकगवेषणलम्बीकृतजलधिजठरप्रविष्टहि मगिरिभुजायमानाया भगवत्या भागीरथ्याः सखी' इति।

*R. G., Kávyalakshaṇa.*

 एवमलङ्कारान्तरमपि शब्दशक्तिमूलानुरणनस्य विषयः। यथा यमुनावर्णनेः—'रविकुलप्रीतिमावहन्ती नरविकुलप्रीतिमावहति। अवारितप्रवाहा सुवारितप्रवाहा'।

*R. G., Ānana II*.

 Jagannátha, however, calls this *Yamunávarṇana* an *ákhyúyiká* in the *Utpreksháprakaraṇa* of the *R. G.,* where he quotes again the first of these two passages thus :—

 आख्यायिकायां जात्यवच्छिन्नस्वरूपोत्प्रेक्षा यथा— "तनयमैनाक, &c."

* (h)* Prof. Maheśachandra Nyáyaratna says of this work :—

 नवीनेषु निबन्धेषु रसगङ्गाधर एव प्रधानम्। अत्र हि नैकोऽपि विषयः (प्रायो) नियुक्तिक उक्तः। प्रत्युत सर्व एव तेऽतीव सूक्ष्मानुसन्धानेन निर्णीताः। (नवीनत्वेऽपि) नातीवाश्लीलतादोषः। नापि रचनायाः काठिन्यम्। यच्च क्वापि क्वापि काठिन्यं दृश्यते तत्प्रतिपाद्यविषयाणां दोषो न ग्रन्थकर्तुः। यानि नवीनान्युदाहरणानि प्रणीतानि तान्यतीव मनोहराणि। ततश्चास्यावलोकने प्रसङ्गादभिनवकाव्यावगतिरपि भवति। इत्येवमस्य बहवो गुणा विद्यन्ते। केवलमेको दोषो यदनेकत्र नैयायिकसमयानुसारितर्केण दूषणभूषणादिकरणमिति। फलतोऽलङ्कारशास्त्रे व्युत्पत्तित्सूनामेतदध्ययन मतीवावश्यकम्।

*Kavyapraká*ś*a, Vijnyapanam.*

 There are in the *Rasagangádhara* two stanzas in which one Ásaf, probably the hero of another of Jagannátha's works, is highly eulogized *(i)*. If this Ásaf be identical with Sháh Jahán’s Khán-khánán of that name, which, I think, highly probable, then we have a means to get at some clue to the date of the composition of the *Rasagangádhara*. For history informs us that that favourite generalissimo of Sháh Jahán died in the year 1641; and one of the stanzas in question refers to Ásaf's death. If, then, we accept the identity of the two Ásafs, it follows that the *Rasagangádhara* was at least still writing in 1641 A. C. *(j).*

 All the copies of this work that I have seen are incomplete, and break off invariably at the same place; and, strangely enough, the break occurs at the third quarter of an *áryá* in the middle of the *Uttaraprakaraṇa (k).* Considering that manuscripts from different parts of the country all coincide in this respect, it is not improbable that the work was never completed by the author himself. Whether its completion was prevented by the author's death, or it was put aside by him for some reason which we do not know, must remain uncertain for the present. I think, it is not safe to indulge in speculation of this kind until we have made sure that the work was left unfinished by the author.

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725036632Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

*(i)* सुधेव वाणी वसुधेव मूर्तिः सुधाकरश्रीसदृशी च कीर्तिः।  
  पयोधिकल्पा मति**रासफेन्दो**र्महीतलेऽन्यस्य न हीति मन्ये ॥

*R. G., Upamáprakaraṇa.*

युक्तं तु याते दिव**मासफेन्दौ** तदाश्रितानां यदभूद्विनाशः।  
इदं तु चित्रं भुवनावकाशे निराश्रया खेलति तस्य कीर्तिः॥

*R. G., Viśeshaprakaraṇa.*

*(j)* See *infra,* p. 17 (o)

*(k)* दिङ्मात्रेणोदाहरणम्।

किं कुर्वते दरिद्राः का सारवती धरा मनोज्ञतरा।  
कः पावनस्त्रिलोक्या.................॥

इति श्रीरसगङ्गाधरे पण्डितराजाभिधानभट्टजगन्नाथविरचितो रसगङ्गाधरः समाप्तः।

 End of the work as found in the MS. belonging to the Bhan Daji Collection, B. B. R. A. Society's Library.

 **Manoramákuchamardana**—This is a work on grammar devoted to a criticism of *Manoramá*, Bhattojídíkshita's commentary on his own *Siddhántakaumudí.* The work is not now accessible to me; but two or three years ago I had an opportunity of seeing the first two leaves of a manuscript of it. I remember that its opening words are *Vireśvaram gurum śesham natvá*. The title of the work, as given there, was *Manoramákuchamardana,* not *Manoramákuchamardiní*, as usually spelt. It will be seen, of course, that the former is a more appropriate title. The Víreśvara Śesha spoken of in the first stanza of the work would appear to be identical with the Víreśvara Śesha under whom Jagannátha's father studied Fatanjali's *Mahábháshya*. But why Jagannátha should call him his own *guru* is not quite clear.

 **Aśvadhátí**—is a small poem of 25 stanzas, called after the metre in which it is composed. It was undertaken by the poet at the request of his grandson, Ráma (*l)*. It is strewn all over with *yamakas* and contains short hymns to various divinities. No quotation from it occurs in the *Rasagangádhara*. This may be merely accidental or may be due to the circumstance that the poem was written after the composition of the *Rasagangádhara.* Moreover, as we have no kind of voucher for saying that our Jagannátha was the author of the poem in question, it is possible that it may have been written by another Jagannátha; because, as will be shown in the sequel, there was a plurality of them. If it really belongs to our author, we know one thing more about him, viz., that he had a grand-son of the name of Ráma.  
** ** **Práṇábharaṇa**—is a small poem, which celebrates the prowess and virtues of a potentate of Kámarúpa, named Práṇanáráyaṇa. It would appear from what purports to be the last but one stanza of the poem that this Práṇanáráyaṇa

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725037424Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

*(l)* रामनाम्नः स्वपौत्रस्य कामनापूरणोत्सुकः।  
        अश्वधाटीं जगन्नाथो विश्वहृद्यामरीरचत् ॥

*Asvadhátí* 6,2.

was a poet himself. The first stanza occurs also in the *Bhámínívilása (m)*, and may possibly have been intended by the author for both the poems. Almost all the other stanzas are found in the *Rasagangádhara*, with a few alterations. Attached to the poem is a gloss by the author himself, which repeats substantially the remarks made in the *Rasagangádhara* on the several stanzas that make up the poem. My conjecture is that this eulogy was prepared by culling several stanzas from the *Rasagangádhara* and making such alterations in them as the occasion required.

** Jagadábharaṇa**—is a panegyric on Dárá Shukoh, Sháh Jahán's eldest son. I have not had access to the poem, and I can only add that Dárá was a patron of Sanskrit letters like Sháh Jahán and his predecessors *(n).*

** Ásaphavilása**—is a prose work, an *ákhyáyiká,* detailing the exploits of one Nabôb Ásaf Khán. I have not seen the book, nor was I aware of its existence until an extract from it was published in the monthly serial, *Kávyamálá.* This Ásaf Khán, as I have already said, must presumably be the same as the Khán-khánán of Sháh Jahán of that name, since we have no record of any other important personage of the same name in the histories of that Emperor's reign. This nobleman's fuller name was Yáminu-d-daula Ásaf Khán; he was promoted to the dignity of Khán-khánán in 1634 and died in 1641 (*o*). We have already remarked that the two stanzas in the *Rasagang*á*dhara* which mention an Ásaf, most probably refer to the hero of this work. In his introduction to the book, Jagannátha tells us that he wrote it at the instance of one Ráyamukunda of the Máthura family *(p)*.

** Bháminívilása**—is a beautiful poem divided into four parts. Like the three *śatakas* of Bhatṛihari it is a compilation

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725038124Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>



*(m) Bh. IV. 42.*

*(n)* See Sir H. Elliot's *History of India,* vol. VII., p. 179, where an interesting account of Dárá's so-called heresy is given.  
*(o)* See Sir H. Elliot's *History of India*, vol. VII., pp. 46, 68, 69.  
*(p)* See the passage quoted *supra* from this work.

of unconnected stanzas, arranged under the four heads of *prástávika, sṛingára, karuṇa,* and *śánta*. 'It is so named possibly after the poet's wife, as Prof. Táránáth suggests *(q)*, or, more probably, because a large portion of it relates to a *bháminí,* a passionate lady; but, perhaps, neither of these explanations may be true. As I have suggested elsewhere on the strength of its last stanza, the poem was probably compiled by the poet, after he had written the *Rasagangádhara*, to protect himself against the danger of plagiarism *(r)*. In fulfilment of his intention, declared at the commencement of the *Rasagang*á*dhara,* Jagannátha drew upon his previous works for illustration wherever he could do so, and, when they did not serve his purpose, composed new verses for the occasion on a variety of subjects. Out of these latter arose the *Bháminívilása.* It should be remarked, however, that this theory renders the incompletion of the *Rasagang*á*dhara* rather difficult of explanation. According to Nágojíbhaṭṭa the poem was written, preparatory to the composition of the *Rasagang*á*dhara*, in order that it might supply a store of suitable illustrations*(s).* This view does not appear to be probable; for the last stanza of the poem, which I see no reason to discard as spurious, militates against it; and it is difficult to conceive that the author could thus exactly foresee his future needs when he had his other works to draw upon. A third theory also may be put forward, viz., that the poem was compiled, not by the author himself, but by some one after him. The second and third theories leave us scope for making the supposition that the completion of the *Rasagangádhara* was prevented by the author's death. Of course, it is impossible to say at present which theory is the correct one.

 These are the hitherto known works of Jagannátha Paṇḍit. It is quite probable that he may have written others which I have yet to be recovered. I am told that he has written a

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725098293Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

*(q)* See his edition of *Bháminívilasá*, p. 1.  
*(r)* See p. 1 of this edition.  
*(s)* उदेति—तत्तदलङ्कारादिलक्ष्यत्वयोग्यं काव्यं भामिनीविलासाख्यम्।

refutation of Appadíkshita's *Chitramímánsá (t)* and a Prákrit poem called *Śaśisená.* I also remember to have noticed, in one of the catalogues of Sanskrit MSS., the entry of a *Paṇḍitarájaśataka* by Jagannátha, which, to judge from the title of the book, must be our poet's production.

 VI. We have yet to notice two more works, the *Vasumatipariṇaya* and the *Ratimanmatha*, which have been attributed to the author of the *Bháminívilása (u)*. Both of them are plays, and bear the name of Jagannátha as their father. I have had access to these plays, and, on an examination of them, I come to the conclusion that both of them are the productions of one and the same author, a Jagannátha, who, however, is not to be identified with our poet. That they were written by the same author is clear from the facts that there are several stanzas common to the two works *(v),* and that the same stanza is employed in both to give the name and parentage of the author *(w)*. We learn from

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725098566Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

Nágojíbhaṭṭá's gloss on निर्माय नूतनम्, &c.

*(t)* Entitled *Chitramímánsákhandana.*  
*(u)* *See Kávyamálá II*. (1, 79).  
*(v)* For instance the following :—

इतो मुखरिता पिकैर्नवरसा रसालच्छटा  
विखण्डितफला शुकैरिह च दाडिमीवीथिका।  
प्रवृत्तशिखिमण्डलाऽत्र च विभाति नीपावलि-  
र्भ्रमद्भ्रमरमालिका बकुलपालिका चाग्रतः॥

*R. M., I.; V. P., II.*

मल्ली सेयमिहान्तिकस्थितमिमं माकन्दमासेवते  
ताम्बूली ननु शोभते समधिकं पूगद्रुमालम्बिनी।  
आलिङ्गत्यधुना लवङ्गलतिका कक्कोलमुच्चैरिदं  
साहित्यं स्पृहणीयभावमयते वल्लीतरूणामपि॥

*R. M., I.; V. P., II.*

सेयं सेयं शशधरमुखी या मया दृष्टपूर्वा  
वित्रस्तैणीचपलनयना चन्द्रिका चेतसो मे।  
मोहो वेत्थं स च मम कथं स्याद्यदस्याः सखीभ्यां  
स्वैरालापः कलयति सुधासम्भृतां श्रोत्रसीमाम्॥

*R. M., I.; V. P., II.*

the prologues to the two plays that the Jagannátha who wrote them was patronized by a petty Maráṭhá chief of the Cholas, and that his father's name was Bálakṛishṇa. The *Vasumatípariṇaya* further informs us that that piece was written by the author during his sojourn in Poona on his way back from Banaras, by command of Balaji Bajirao, the then reigning Peshwa, and that it was there put to the stage on the occasion of the annual festival in honour of Ganapati *(x)*.

 In this account there are three items which, put together, conclusively disprove the identity of the two authors. Firstly, there is a difference in the names of their fathers; secondly, the one was Poet Laureate to Emperor Sháh Jahán while the other was patronized by a chief of Southern India; and lastly,

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725099436Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

*(w)* अन्येद्रं जगदस्थितेन्द्रमपि वा कर्तुं प्रगल्भेऽन्वये  
 सञ्जातो ननु बालकृष्णसचिवोत्तंसस्य रूपान्तरम्।  
 लक्ष्म्यम्बाहृदयाब्धिशीतकिरणः प्रेम्णाऽधिगम्यः सता-  
 मस्ति न्यस्तपदो गुणैरिह जगन्नाथाभिधानः सुधीः॥

* (x) *"तेन च निजोपजीव्यस्य भृशबलोपनामकस्य निखिलमहीमण्डलनिचोलायमानचोलनीवृदाखण्डलस्य चण्डतरनिजप्रतापितारिपुनृपसिंहस्य श्रीमतः प्रतापसिंहनेतुरनुज्ञया समासाद्य तावदाशीविषभूषणराजधानीं प्रकाशोकृतविमुक्तसम्पदं श्रीमतीं काशीं प्रतिनिवृत्तेन सम्प्रत्यस्यां पुण्यविशेषवितरणगरीयस्यां पुण्यनगर्यामधिगतप्रधानविभुप्रसादेन तन्निदेशतः प्रणीतं निखिलराजोपादेयहेयगुणागुणविशेषवर्णनचमत्कृतमिदं नाटकं प्रचारयितव्यमिति विविधदेशसञ्चारसञ्जातसौहृदस्य मम हस्ते समर्पितम्। "  
 "आर्ये समादिष्टोस्मि............................ सकलकलाकलापनिधिनाऽनन्यसामान्यधिषणागुणातिशयितधिषणयोः पराक्रमोर्जस्वलपराक्रमप्रक्रमजनितप्राचीनप्रवीरलाघवयोः सदाशिवरायरघुनाथरायनामधेय-योरग्रजानुवर्तनपराकृतभरतबिडौजस्तनुजयोरनुजयोर्विन्यस्तसमस्तकार्यधुरतया विश्रान्तचेतसा श्रीशिवनृपच्छत्रपतिकुलप्रधानेन सुगुणसमुदयनिधानेन श्रीमतो राजीवबन्धुसदृशतेजसो बाजीरायप्रभुवर्यस्य नन्दनेन बालाजिरायमहीसङ्क्रन्दनेन यथा भोः कलाधर भवता भगवतः श्री महागणपतेरेतस्मिन् महोत्सवे वार्षिके समवेता इमे रसिका विपश्चितो वयं च केनचिदभिनवेन नयगुणशृङ्गारितेन शृङ्गाररसशृङ्गाटकेन नाटकेन विनोदयितव्या इति।”

*Vasumatíp., Act I.*

 The V.P. concludes by invoking a blessing on Balaji Bajirao thus :—

मोदन्तां शिथिलीभवत्खलजनं वर्णा द्विजन्मादयः  
स्वैरोन्मीलितसस्यजातसुभगं वर्षन्तु वर्षाघनाः।  
वीरोदारसुधीगृहेषु विहतिं बध्नातु लोकप्रसू-  
राचन्द्रार्कमयं सुखी विजयतां **बालाजिरायः** प्रभुः॥

the one lived in the middle of the 17th century, whereas the other flourished in the time of Balaji Bajirao, that is, about the middle of the 18th century. It is to be noted, likewise, that Jagannátha Tarkapanchánana, the author of the *Vivádabhaṇgárṇava,* was a third writer different from Paṇḍitarája Jagannátha as well as from the author of the two plays *(y).*

 VII. Of all Sanskrit authors Jagannátha was peculiarly subject to the jealousies and irritabilities of the scribbling race. Appadíkshita and Bhaṭṭojídíkshita, who were probably contemporaneous with him (*z*), appear to have been his great literary rivals. The former he has held up to the ridicule of the reading world in very strong language. In the *Rasagang*á*dhara* he is denied the respect due to an adversary worthy of esteem, and his works are severely criticized and totally condemned. Jagannátha showers on him, in a half-sarcastic tone, such epithets as *áyúshmán, draviḍaśiromaṇi, draviḍapungava* and, in one place, takes a liberty at which any gentleman of good breeding would blush *(a)*. No doubt, his

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725102103Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

* * *(y)* See the opening stanza of the *Vivádabhangárṇava* where the author gives Rudra as his father's name.

 (*z*) A *champú*, entitled नीलकण्ठविजय, written by a relative of Appadíkshita, gives 1637 A. C. as the date of its composition. The *Kavicharitra* gives Ayyádíkshita as the name of the author of this *champú,* and adds that he was Appadíkshita's nephew (p. 119), whereas the *Kávyamalá* states that it was composed by Nílakanṭha, who was grandson either to Appadíkshita himself or te his brother. As I have not seen the book I am not in a position to decide between the conflicting statements. But it seems to me that Jagannátha's invective against and personal abuse of Appadíkshita can be satisfactorily explained only on the ground of their contemporaneity; and in this light the statement of the *Kavicharitra* that the author was Appadíkshita's nephew appears more probable; for it is more natural to suppose that Appadíkshita and his nephew were both living in 1637 when the latter wrote his work. To Bhaṭṭojídíkshita's date I have not been able to get any clue.

* (a)* नेदं रूपकम्। रूपके च बिम्बप्रतिबिम्बभावो नास्तीति केनाप्यालङ्कारिकम्मन्येन प्रतारितस्य दीर्घश्रवस उक्तिरश्रद्धेयैव।

*Rúpakaprakaraṇa.*

.... दीर्घश्रवसो लम्बकर्णस्य द्रविडस्याप्पदीक्षितस्य।

Nágoji's gloss on the above.

criticism is often just, but he takes delight in employing unnecessarily severe language, and sometimes betrays unmistakable signs of malice *(b)*. As to Bhattojídíkshita I am told that a commentator of the *Bháminívilása* refers the second stanza of that poem to Jagannátha's rivalries with him. If a copy of the *Manoramákuchamardana* be discovered, I have no doubt that it will throw much light on the point.

 His excessive egotism is another trait of character peculiar to Jagannátha. In some Sanskrit authors we find some selflaudatory sentences, but none has given so free and unreserved expression to his feeling of self-importance. Indeed, when we read the opening stanzas of the *Rasagangádhara* and the closing ones of the *Bháminívilása* we recognize a voice that speaks from a full consciousness of its own worth, and we are almost ready to excuse the poet; but one cannot help thinking that such vaunts as his, rather indicate an indelicacy of feeling and an unbecoming love of self-praise.

 As a poet Jagannátha takes a high rank, and may be classed with Kálidása, Bhavabhúti and other writers of celebrity. He is essentially a poet of emotions, and has achieved a high measure of success in his department. Though he belongs to the degenerate times of Sanskrit poetry, he is almost free from the affectation and extravagance of his age. In sweetness of melody and perspicuity of diction he stands on a level with Bilhaṇa and Jayadeva. *Prasáda,* as he himself tells us, is a special characteristic of his poetry (*c)*. As a writer of prose and a controversialist Jagannátha, perhaps, stands second to none but the great Śankara. His prose is racy, vigorous, and characterized by the same perspicuity which pervades his poetry. He is thoroughly acquainted with the use of the

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725103085Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

* (b)* See, for instance, the uncalled for discussion on the formation of पुरतः in the *Upamáprakaraṇa.*

* (c)* श्रुतमात्रा वाक्यार्थं करतलबदरमिव निवेदयन्ती घटना प्रसादस्य। अयं च सर्वसाधारणो गुणः। उदाहरणान्यत्र प्रायशो मदीयानि सर्वाण्येव पद्यानि।

*R. G., Anana I*.

offensive and defensive weapons of controversy and wields them with admirable effect. The *Rasagangádhara* is full of highy argumentative passages which it is a treat to peruse.

 VIII. In the foregoing pages I have tried to avoid theorising as far as possible. I know that an attempt may be made to spell out a biography of the author from several passages of the *Bháminívilása;* and I am also aware that many a theory may be based on some of the anecdotes given above and on the incomplete nature of the hitherto discovered Mss. of the *Rasagangádhara;* but I think that such theories are as likely to prove wrong as right and cannot be accepted without any corroborative testimony. The safest course is to wait for more facts.

**अथ भामिनीविलासे**  
**प्रास्ताविकविलासः।**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1724684737500.png"/>

**माधुर्यपरमसीमा सारस्वतजलधिमथनसम्भूता।  
पिबतामनल्पसुखदा वसुधायां मम सुधाकविता॥१॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725103598Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

निधाय हृदि विश्वेशं नत्वा विद्यागुरून् गुरून्।  
नानाग्रन्थान् समालोच्य पाठभेदान् विविच्य च॥१॥  
यः पण्डितधुरीणेन जगन्नाथेन निर्मितः।  
श्रीभामिनीविलासाख्यः प्रबन्धो भुवि विश्रुतः॥२॥  
रसिकाह्लादजननं तं व्याख्यातुं यथामति।  
यते लक्ष्मणशर्माहं वैद्यवंशसमुद्भवः॥३॥  
त्यज्यते नात्र दुर्बोधं नानपेक्षितमुच्यते।  
काव्यमर्मप्रकाशाय परो यत्नो विधीयते॥४॥  
दृष्टं किमपि लोकेस्मिन्न दोषपरिवर्जितम्।  
तदत्र स्खलितं यत्तत्सहध्वं विबुधोत्तमाः॥५॥

पण्डितराजेन रसगङ्गाधरे

निर्माय नूतनमुदाहरणानुरूपं  
काव्यं मयात्र निहितं न परस्य किञ्चित्।  
किं सेव्यते सुमनसां मनसापि गन्धः  
कस्तूरिकाजननशक्तिभृता मृगेण॥

इति ग्रन्थादौ कृतां प्रतिज्ञां परिपालयता ये सरसा नूतनाः श्लोका निर्मायोदाहरणतया निहिता अन्ये च ये स्फुटश्लोकाः प्रसङ्गवशाद्रचितास्तेषामन्यैरात्मकृतत्वख्यापनपरिहारायैकत्र सङ्कलनेनेदं विलासचतुष्टयात्मकमुत्कृष्टं भामिनीविलासाख्यं काव्यं निबद्धमित्यस्यैव काव्यस्यान्तिमपद्यादनुमीयते। अस्य प्रास्ताविकाख्ये प्रथमे विलासे प्रायोऽन्योक्तय

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725103816Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

 1—Given in the appendix by B. and omitted by C, E, F

**दिगन्ते श्रूयन्ते मदमलिनगण्डाः करटिनः  
करिण्यः कारुण्यास्पदमसमशीलाः खलु मृगाः।**

**इदानीं लोकेऽस्मिन्ननुपमशिखानां पुनरयं  
नखानां पाण्डित्यं प्रकटयतु कस्मिन् मृगपतिः॥२॥**

**पुरा सरसि मानसे विकचसारसालिस्खलत्–  
परागसुरभीकृते पयसि यस्य यातं वयः।  
स पल्वलजलेऽधुना मिलदनेकभेकाकुले  
मरालकुलनायकः कथय रे कथं वर्तताम्॥३॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725171804Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

एवैकत्र सङ्कलिताः। अस्य विलासस्यान्योक्तिविलास इति यन्नाम केषुचित्पुस्तकेषु दृश्यते तदप्येतन्मूलकमेवेति भाति। प्रास्ताविकविलास इति नाम त्वन्येषां सुभाषितश्लोकानामपीह सत्त्वादनुरूपतरम्। शृङ्गाराख्ये द्वितीये विलासे शृङ्गारप्रचुराणि करुणाख्ये तृतीये करुणरसप्रधानानि शान्ताख्ये चतुर्थे च शान्तरसोद्बोधकानीह पद्यानि निबद्धानि। काव्यस्य भामिनीविलास इति सञ्ज्ञा भामिन्याः स्वभार्याया विलासमुद्दिश्य कृतेति तारानाथशर्मणामभिप्रायः। वस्तुतस्तु सञ्ज्ञाबीजं न निश्चयेन ज्ञायत इति वक्तव्यम्।

(१) पिबतां पानं कुर्वताम्। पिबतामित्यनेनान्यथान्वयासम्भवात् सुधाकवितेति विशेषणसमास एव ग्राह्यः।

(२) इयमप्रस्तुतप्रशंसा यां जना अन्योक्तिं प्राहुः। अप्रस्तुतव्यवहारेण प्रस्तुतव्यवहारो यत्र वर्ण्यते साऽप्रस्तुतप्रशंसा। इयं पञ्चधा भवति। अप्रस्तुतेन प्रस्तुतं गम्यते यस्यामित्येका। कार्येण कारणमित्यपरा। कारणेन कार्यमिति तृतीया। सामान्येन विशेष इति चतुर्थी। विशेषेण सामान्यमिति पञ्चमी। अस्मिन् पद्ये स्ववृत्तान्त एव कविना प्रस्तुतत्वेन विवक्षित इति वदन्ति। करटिनो दन्तिनः। दिगन्ते श्रूयन्त इत्यनेन तेषां पलायनं ध्वनितम्। कारुण्यास्पदत्वे स्त्रीत्वं हेतुः। असमशीला विषमस्वभावाः। तुच्छा इति यावत्। पाण्डित्यं विदारणरूपस्वकर्मकौशलम्।

( ३ ) सारसालिः कमलपङ्क्तिः। भेको मण्डूकः। मरालो हंसः।

**तृष्णालोलविलोचने कलयति प्राचीं चकोरीगणे  
मौनं मुञ्चति किं च कैरवकुले कामे धनुर्धुन्वति।  
माने मानवतीजनस्य सपदि प्रस्थातुकामेऽधुना  
धातः किं नु विधौ विधातुमुचितो धाराधराडम्बरः॥४॥  
अयि दलदरविन्द स्यन्दमानं मरन्दं  
तव किमपि लिहन्तो मञ्जु गुञ्जन्तु भृङ्गाः।  
दिशि दिशि निरपेक्षस्तावकीनं विवृण्वन्  
परिमलमयमन्यो बान्धवो गन्धवाहः॥५॥  
समुपागतवति दैवादवहेलां कुटज मधुकरे मागाः।  
मकरन्दतुन्दिलानामरविन्दानामयं महामान्यः॥६॥  
तावत्कोकिल विरसान् यापय दिवसान्वनान्तरे निवसन्।  
यावन्मिलदलिमालः कोऽपि रसालः समुल्लसति॥७॥  
कमलिनि मलिनीकरोषि चेत**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725172216Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

(४) कलयतीत्यादि सत्सप्तम्यन्तम्। कलयति चन्द्रिकापानार्थं स्वीकुर्वति। मौनं मुञ्चति सङ्कोचं त्यजति। कैरवं चन्द्रविकास्यः सितोत्पलजातिविशेषः। धुन्वति टङ्कारयति। मानः पुरुषकृतापराधप्रकाशकश्चेष्टाविशेषः। धाराधराडम्बरो मेघाच्छादनम्।

(५) दलदरविन्द विकसितकमल। कमप्यनिर्वचनीयम्। अतिमधुरमित्यर्थः। अन्यस्त्वदीयरससेवनासक्तभ्रमरापेक्षया विलक्षणः। भ्रमराणां मकरन्दलाभेन कृत्रिमबन्धुत्वं भवेन्नाम। गन्धवाहस्य तूपकारलाभाभावेनाकृत्रिमबन्धुत्वमतिश्लाघ्यमिति भावः।

(६) मकरन्दतुन्दिलानां पुष्परसपरिपूरितानाम्।

(७) विरसान् स्वाभिमतप्रयोजनशून्यान्। कथमपि कालक्षेपं कुर्विति भावार्थः। मिलदलिमालः सम्प्राप्तभ्रमरसङ्घः। रसालश्चूतवृक्षः।

(८) मलिनीकरोषि सखेदं करोषि। परिणतः परिपक्वः। मार्मिका मर्मज्ञाः।

**किमिति बकैरवहेलितानभिज्ञैः।  
परिणतमकरन्दमार्मिकास्ते  
जगति भवन्तु चिरायुषो मिलिन्दाः॥८॥  
नितरां नीचोऽस्मीति त्वं खेदं कूप मा कदापि कृथाः।  
अत्यन्तसरसहृयो यतः परेषां गुणग्रहीतासि॥ ९॥  
येनामन्दमरन्दे दलदरविन्दे दिनान्यनाषित।  
कुटजे खलु तेनेहा तेने हा मधुकरेण कथम्॥१०॥  
अयि मलयज महिमायं कस्य गिरामस्तु विषयस्ते।  
उद्गिरतो यद्गरलं फणिनः पुष्णासि परिमलोद्गारैः॥११॥  
पाटीर तव पटीयान् कः परिपाटीमिमामुरीकर्तुम्।  
यत्पिंषतामपि नृणां पिष्टोऽपि तनोषि परिमलैः पुष्टिम्॥१२॥  
नीरक्षीरविवेके हंसालस्यं त्वमेव तनुषे चेत्।**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725172956Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

मिलिन्दा भ्रमराः। येषां रसिकत्वमेव नास्ति तेषामवहेलनया न कापि हानिरतो न खेदः कार्यः। ये मार्मिकास्ते चिरायुषश्चेत् त्वया सर्व मेव प्राप्तमिति तात्पर्यार्थः।

(९) नीचो निम्नो हीनश्च। सरसहृदयः सजलाभ्यन्तरः सरसान्तःकरणश्च। गुणः कलशाकर्षणरज्जुः कलाप्रावीण्यं च। श्लिष्टविशेषणेयमप्रस्तुतप्रशंसा।

(१०) अमन्दमरन्दे परिपूर्णमकरन्दे। हा तेन मधुकरेण कुटजे कथमीहा ते इत्यन्वयः। ईहा स्पृहा। तेने चक्रे।

(११) कस्य गिरां विषयोस्तु। न कस्यापीत्यर्थः। परिमलोद्गारैर्गन्धविशेषप्रवाहैः। विषं वमतो सर्पानपि स्वगन्धेन तर्पयसीत्यहो ते महिमेत्यर्थः।

(१२) पाटीर चन्दन। परिपाटीं रीतिम्। उरीकर्तुं स्वीकर्तुम्। पिंषतां चूर्णयताम्। घर्षयतामिति यावत्। अस्य तात्पर्यार्थस्तु (११) पद्यस्येव।

(१३) विवेके विवेचने। पृथक्करण इति यावत्। त्वमेवेत्येवकारेणेतरस्यविवेकित्वं

**विश्वस्मिन्नधुनान्यः कुलव्रतं पालयिष्यति कः॥१३॥  
उपरि करवालधाराकाराः क्रूरा भुजङ्गमपुङ्गवात्।  
अन्तःसाक्षाद्द्राक्षादीक्षागुरवो जयन्ति केऽपि जनाः॥१४॥  
स्वच्छन्द दलदरविन्द ते मरन्दं  
विन्दतो विदधतु गुञ्जितं मिलिन्दाः।  
आमोदानथ हरिदन्तराणि नेतुं  
नैवान्यो जगति समीरणात्प्रवीणः॥१५॥  
याते मय्यचिरान्निदाघमिहिरज्वालाशतैः शुष्कतां  
गन्ता कं प्रति पान्थसन्ततिरसौ सन्तापमालाकुला।  
एवं यस्य निरन्तराधिपटलैर्नित्यं वपुः क्षीयते  
धन्यं जीवनमस्य मार्गसरसो धिग्वारिधीनां जनुः॥१६॥  
आपेदिरेऽम्बरपथं परितः पतङ्गा  
भृङ्गा रसालकुसुमानि समाश्रयन्ते।  
सङ्कोचमञ्चति सरस्त्वयि दीनदीनो  
मीनो नु हन्त कतमां गतिमभ्युपैतु॥१७॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725173506Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

नास्तीति सूच्यते। विश्वस्मिन् त्रैलोक्ये। कुलव्रतं तवेति शेषः।

(१४) उपरि बहिः। करवालधाराकाराः खड्गधारावत्तीक्ष्णाः। भुजङ्गमपुङ्गवान्महाभुजङ्गमात्। द्राक्षाया दीक्षायाः शीतलत्वमाधुर्यादिरूपाया गुरव उपदेष्टारः। केप्यनिर्वचनीयमहिमानः। उल्लेखालङ्कारोयमुपमाव्यतिरेकाभ्यां तयोः समुच्चयेन च सङ्कीर्णः।

(१५) मिलिन्दा भ्रमराः। हरिदन्तराणि दिगन्तराणि। अयं श्लोकः (५) पद्येन समानार्थकः।

(१६) निदाघमिहिरो ग्रीष्मसूर्यः। गन्ता गमिष्यति। आधिर्मानसी व्यथा। जीवनं जीवितं जलं च।

(१७) आपेदिरे पूर्वमेव गताः। पतङ्गाः पक्षिणः। रसाल आम्रः।

**मधुप इव मारुतेऽस्मिन् मा सौरभलोभमम्बुजिनि मंस्थाः।  
लोकानामेव मुदे महितोऽप्यात्मामुनार्थितां नीतः॥१८॥  
गुञ्जति मञ्जु मिलिन्दे मा मालति मौनमुपयासीः।  
शिरसा वदान्यगुरवः सादरमेनं वहति सुरतरवः॥१९॥  
यैस्त्वं गुणगणवानपि सतां द्विजिह्वैरसेव्यतां नीतः।  
तानपि वहसि पटीरज किं कथयामस्त्वदीयमौन्नत्यम्॥२०॥  
गाहितमखिलं गहनं परितो दृष्टाश्च विटपिनः सर्वे।  
सहकार न प्रपेदे मधुपेन भवत्समं जगति॥२१॥  
अपनीतपरिमलान्तरकथे पदं न्यस्य देवतरुकुसुमे।  
पुष्पान्तरेऽपि गन्तुं वाञ्छसि चेत् भ्रमर धन्योऽसि॥२२॥  
तटिनि चिराय विचारय विन्ध्यभुवस्तव पवित्रायाः।  
शुष्यन्त्या अपि युक्तं किं खलु रथ्योदकादानम्॥२३॥  
पत्रफलपुष्पलक्ष्म्या कदाप्यदृष्टं वृतं च खलु शूकैः।**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725174266Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

सङ्कोचमञ्चति शुष्कत्वं याति। दीनदीनोत्यन्तदीनः।

(१८) अम्बुजिनि कमलिनि। महितः श्रेष्ठः। अर्थितां नीतो याचकतां प्रापितः। लघुत्वं स्वीकृतमिति यावत्। परोपकारायैवायं त्वां सौरभं याचते न लोभादित्यर्थः।

(१९) मौनमप्रफुल्लीभावं मूकभावं च। वदान्यगुरवो दातृश्रेष्ठाः।

(२०) द्विजिह्वैः सर्पैः। पिशुनैरिति च गम्यते। पटीरज चन्दनतरो।

(२१) गाहितं विचितम्। गहनं वनम्।

(२२) अपनीता दूरीकृता परिमलान्तरकथा येन तस्मिन्। धन्योसीत्युपालम्भः। पुष्पान्तरं वाञ्छसि चेद्धिक् त्वामिति भावः।

(२३) विन्ध्यभुवो विन्ध्यपर्वतप्रसूताया अतएव पवित्रायाः।

(२४) शूकैः कण्टकैर्वृतं व्याप्तम्। बर्बुरो बाभळी इति प्रसिद्धो वृक्षः।

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725174430Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

 21—Omitted in D. E. F.

**उपसर्पेम भवन्तं बर्बुर वद कस्य लोभेन॥२४॥  
एकस्त्वं गहनेऽस्मिन् कोकिल न कलं कदाचिदपि कुर्याः।  
साजात्यशङ्कयाऽमी न त्वां निघ्नन्ति निर्दयाः काकाः॥२५॥  
तरुकुलसुषमापहरां जनयन्तीं जगति जीवजातार्तिम्।  
केन गुणेन भवानीतात हिमानीमिमां वहसि॥२६॥  
कलभ तवान्तिकमागतमलिमेनं मा कदाप्यवज्ञासीः।  
अपि दानसुन्दराणां द्विपधुर्याणामयं शिरोधार्यः॥२७॥  
अमरतरुकुसुमसौरभसेवनसम्पूर्णसकलकामस्य।  
पुष्पान्तरसेवेयं भ्रमरस्य विडम्बना महती॥२८॥  
पृष्टाः खलु परपुष्टाः परिनो दृष्टाश्च विटपिनः सर्वे।  
माकन्द न प्रपेदे मधुपेन तवोपमा जगति॥२९॥  
तोयैरल्पैरपि करुणया भीमभानौ निदाघे  
मालाकार व्यरचि भवता या तरोरस्य पुष्टिः।  
सा किं शक्या जनयितुमिह प्रावृषेण्येन वारां  
धारासारानपि विकिरता विश्वतो वारिदेन॥३०॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725174704Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

(२५) कलं मधुरारावम्। साजात्यशङ्कया सजातीयोयमस्माकमिति धिया। कलं करोषि चेद् वैजात्यं ज्ञात्वा त्वामिमे हन्युरेवेत्यर्थः।

(२६) सुषमा शोभा। जीवजातार्तिं प्राणिसमूहपीडाम्। भवानीतात हिमालय। हिमानीं हिमसंहतिम्। न तवेदमुचितमिति भावः।

(२७) कलभ गजशिशो। द्विपधुर्या गजश्रेष्ठाः।

(२८) इदं पद्यं (२२) पद्येन समानार्थकम्।

(२९) परपुष्टाः कोकिलाः। इदं (२१) पद्येन समानार्थकम्।

(३०) अल्पैस्तोयैरर्थात् कूपाद्युद्धृतैः। भीमो भानुर्यस्मिन् तस्मिन्निदाघे ग्रीष्मे। प्रावृषेण्येन वर्षाकालिकेन। विश्वतः सर्वतः।

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725174733Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

 24- Omitted in A.

**आरामाधिपतिर्विवेकविकलो नूनं रसा नीरसा  
वात्याभिः परुषीकृता दश दिशश्चण्डातपो दुःसहः।  
एवं धन्वनि चम्पकस्य सकले संहारहेतावपि  
त्वं सिञ्चन्नमृतेन तोयद कुतोऽप्याविष्कृतो वेधसा॥३१॥  
न यत्र स्थेमानं दधुरतिभयत्रान्तनयना  
गलद्दानोद्रेकभ्रमदलिकदम्बाः करटिनः।  
लुठन्मुक्ताभारे भवति परलोकं गतवतो  
हरेरद्य द्वारे शिव शिव शिवानां कलकलः॥३२॥  
दधानः प्रेमाणं तरुषु समभावेन विपुलां  
न मालाकारोऽसावकृत करुणां बालबकुले।  
अयं तु द्रागुद्यत्कुसुमनिकराणां परिमलै  
र्दिगन्तानातेने मधुपकुलझङ्कारभरितान् ॥ ३३ ॥  
मूलं स्थूलमतीव बन्धनदृढं शारवाः शतं मांसला  
वासो दुर्गमहीधरे तरुपते कुत्रास्ति भीतिस्तव।  
एकः किं तु मनागयं जनयति स्वान्ते ममाधिज्वरं**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725194413Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

(३१) वात्याभिर्वातसमूहैः। धन्वनि मरुभूमौ। अमृतेन जलेन।

(३२) यत्र यस्मिन् द्वारे। स्थेमानं स्थिरत्वम्। गलद्दानं स्रवन्मदोदकं तस्योद्रेकोतिशयस्तेन भ्रमन्तोलिकदम्बा भ्रमरसङ्घा येषु तथाविधाः। हरेर्द्वारे शिवानां कलकलो भवतीत्यन्वयः। शिव शिवेति खेदे।

(३३) तरुषु स्वीयेष्विति शेषः। बालबकुले विपुलां करुणां नाकृतेत्यन्वयः। द्राग् झटिति। उद्यतामुदयं प्राप्नुवतां कुसुमानां निकराः समूहास्तेषाम्। झङ्कारो गुञ्जारवः।

(३४) शतमित्युपलक्षणम्। तेन बह्व्य इत्यर्थः। मांसलाः पुष्टाः। दुर्गमहीधरे दुर्गमपर्वते। तव भीतिः कुत्रास्ति। यन्निमित्ता भीतिस्तन्न पश्याम

**ज्वालालीवलयीभवन्नकरुणो दावानलो घस्मरः॥३४॥  
ग्रीष्मे भीष्मतरैः करैर्दिनकृता दग्धोऽपि यश्चातक  
स्त्वां ध्यायन् घन वासरान् कथमपि द्राघीयसो नीतवान्।  
दैवाल्लोचनगोचरेण भवता तस्मिन्निदानीं यदि  
स्वीचक्रे करकानिपातनकृपा तत् कं प्रति ब्रूमहे॥३५॥  
दवदहनजटालज्वालजालाहतानां  
परिगलितलतानां म्लायतां भूरुहाणाम्।  
अयि जलधर शैलश्रेणिशृङ्गेषु तोयं  
वितरसि बहु कोऽयं श्रीमदस्तावकीनः॥३६॥  
शृण्वन् पुरः परुषगर्जितमस्य हन्त  
रे पान्थ विह्वलमना न मनागपि स्याः।  
विश्वार्त्तिवारणसमर्पितजीवनोऽयं  
नाकर्णितः किमु सखे भवताम्बुवाहः॥३७॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725194999Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

इत्यर्थः। एकः केवलः। मनागीषत्। आधिज्वरं चिन्तातापम्। ज्वालालीवलयीभवञ् ज्वालामण्डलरूप इत्यर्थः। घस्मरो भक्षकः।

(३५) दिनकृता सूर्येण। द्राघीयसो दीर्घतरान्। करका वर्षोपलः॥ कृपेति सोल्लुण्ठम्। तेन निर्दयत्वमित्यर्थः।

(३६) जटालः सङ्घीभूतः। ज्वालो ज्वाला। भूरुहाणां म्लायतां सतामित्यन्वयः। इयमनादरे षष्ठी। तेन म्लानीभवतो वृक्षाननादृत्येत्यर्थः। श्रीमदो जलसम्पत्तिमदः। लक्ष्मीमद इत्यपि ध्वन्यते।

(३७) विश्वार्तिवारणाय समर्पितं जीवनं येन तथाविधः। जीवनं जलं जीवितं च। भवतायं विश्वार्तिवारणसमर्पितजीवनो नाकर्णितः किमित्यन्वयः। अस्योपकृतय एव गर्जितत्वमिति भावः।

**सौरभ्यं भुवनत्रयेऽपि विदितं शैत्यं तु लोकोत्तरं  
कीर्तिः किं च दिगङ्गनाङ्गणगता किं त्वेतदेकं शृणु।  
सर्वानेव गुणानियं निगिरति श्रीखण्ड ते सुन्दरा-  
नुज्झन्ती खलु कोटरेषु गरलज्वालां द्विजिह्वावली॥३८॥  
नापेक्षा न च दाक्षिण्यं न प्रीतिर्न च सङ्गतिः।  
तथापि हरते तापं लोकानामुन्नतो घनः॥३९॥  
समुत्पत्तिः स्वच्छे सरसि हरिहस्ते निवसति  
र्निवासः पद्मायाः सुरहृदयहारी परिमलः।  
गुणैरेतैरन्यैरपि च ललितस्याम्बुज तव  
द्विजोत्तंसे हंसे यदि रतिरतीवोन्नतिरियम्॥४०॥  
साकं ग्रावगणैर्लुठन्ति मणयस्तीरेऽर्कबिम्बोपमा  
नीरे नीरचरैः समं स भगवान्निद्राति नारायणः।  
एवं वीक्ष्य तवाविवेकमथ च प्रौढिं परामुन्नतेः  
किं निन्दान्यथवा स्तवानि कथय क्षीरार्णव त्वामहम्॥४१॥  
किं खलु रत्नैरेतैः किं पुनरभ्रायितेन वपुषा ते।  
सलिलमपि यन्न तावकमर्णव वदनं प्रयाति तृषितानाम् ॥४२॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725195395Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

(३८) तु निश्चयेन। निगिरत्युद्वमति। लोपयतीति यावत्। श्रीखण्ड चन्दन।

(३९) अपेक्षा प्रत्युपकारादिवाञ्छा। दाक्षिण्यमानुकूल्यम्। तथाप्य पेक्षादितापहरणहेत्वभावेपि। उन्नत उच्चदेशस्थित उदारप्रकृतिश्च।

(४०) हरिहस्ते विष्णुहस्ते सूर्यकरे वा। निवासो वासस्थानभूतत्वम्। ललितस्य मण्डितस्य। द्विजोत्तंसे पक्षिश्रेष्ठे। ब्राह्मणवर इति च ध्वन्यते। अतीवोन्नतिः परं माहात्म्यम्।

(४१) महान्तोपि क्षीरार्णवमाश्रयन्त इति तस्यौन्नत्यम्। स तु यथोचितोपचारं न करोतीत्यविवेकिता।

(४२) अभ्रायितेनाभ्रवन्नीलेन।

**इयत्यां सम्पत्तावपि च सलिलानां त्वमधुना  
न तृष्णामार्त्तानां हरसि यदि कासार सहसा।  
निदाघे चण्डांशौ किरति परितोऽङ्गारनिकरं  
कृशीभूतः केषामहह परिहर्तासि खलु ताम्॥४३॥  
अयि रोषमुरीकरोषि नो चेत्  
किमपि त्वां प्रति वारिधे वदामः।  
जलदेन तवार्थिना विमुक्ता–  
न्यपि तोयानि महान् न हा जहासि॥४४॥  
न वारयामो भवतीं विशन्तीं वर्षानदि स्रोतसि जह्नुजायाः।  
न युक्तमेतत्तु पुरो यदस्यास्तरङ्गभङ्गान् प्रकटीकरोषि॥४५॥  
पौलोमीपतिकानने विलसतां गीर्वाणभूमीरुहां  
येनाघ्रातसमुज्झितानि कुसुमान्याजघ्निरे निर्जरैः।  
तस्मिन्नद्य मधुव्रते विधिवशान्माध्वीकमाकाङ्क्षति  
त्वं चेदञ्चसि लोभमम्बुज तदा किं त्वां प्रति ब्रूमहे॥४६॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725195817Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

(४३) कासार सरोवर। तां तृष्णाम्।

(४४) अपिर्भिन्नक्रमः। तेन महानपीत्यन्वयः । हेति खेदे।

(४५) जह्नुजाया भागीरथ्याः। यस्याश्रयणं कार्यं तेनैव सह विरोधप्रकटनमत्यन्तासमीचीनमिति भावः।

(४६) पौलोमीपतिकानने नन्दनवने। पौलोमीन्द्राणी। आघ्रातसमुज्झितान्यादावाघ्रातानि पश्चात् समुज्झितानि। येन मधुव्रतेन। अस्याघ्रातसमुज्झितानीत्यनेन सम्बन्धः। गीर्वाणभूमीरुहां कल्पवृक्षाणाम्। मधुव्रतो भ्रमरः। विधिवशाद्दुर्दैववशात्। माध्वीकं मधु।

**भुक्ता मृणालपटली भवता निपीता–  
न्यम्बूनि यत्र नलितानि निषेवितानि।  
रे राजहंस वद तस्य सरोवरस्य  
कृत्येन केन भवितासि कृतोपकारः॥४७॥  
प्रारम्भे कुसुमाकरस्य परितो यस्योल्लसन्मञ्जरी–  
पुञ्जे मञ्जुलगुञ्जितानि रचयंस्तानातनोरुत्सवान्।  
तस्मिन्नद्य रसालशाखिनि दशां दैवात्कृशामञ्चति  
त्वं चेन्मुञ्चसि चञ्चरीक विनयं नीचस्त्वदन्योऽस्ति कः॥४८॥  
एणीगणेषु गुरुगर्वनिमीलिताक्षः  
किं कृष्णसार खलु खेलसि काननेऽस्मिन्।  
सीमामिमां कलय भिन्नकरीन्द्रकुम्भ–  
मुक्तामयीं हरिविहारवसुन्धरायाः॥४९॥  
जठरज्वलनज्वलताप्यपगतशङ्कं समागतापि पुरः।  
करिणामरिणा हरिणा हरिणाली हन्यतां नु कथम्॥५०॥  
येन भिन्नकरिकुम्भविस्खलन्–  
मौक्तिकावलिभिरञ्चिता मही।**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725196195Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

(४७) मृणालपटली मृणालसङ्घः।

(४८) कुसुमाकरस्य वसन्तस्य। ताननुभूतान्। चञ्चरीक भ्रमर। विनयः कृतज्ञताबुद्धिः। चतुर्थचरणेऽनुप्रासालङ्कारः।

(४९) एणीगणेषु हरिणीसङ्घेषु।

(५०) जठरज्वलनज्वलता जठराग्निना तप्यमानेन। क्षुधार्तेनेत्यर्थः। अपगतशङ्कं निःशङ्कम्। अनेनानायासप्राप्यता दर्शिता। द्वितीयार्धे यमकं स्पष्टमेव।

(५१) अञ्चिता भूषिता । पराक्रमः स्वीय इति शेषः।

**अद्य तेन हरिणान्तिके कथं  
कथ्यतां नु हरिणा पराक्रमः॥५१॥  
स्थितिं नो रे दध्याः क्षणमपि मदान्धेक्षण सखे  
गजश्रेणीनाथ त्वमिह जटिलायां वनभुवि।  
असौ कुम्भिभ्रान्त्या खरनखरविद्रावितमहा–  
गुरुग्रावग्रामः स्वपिति गिरिगर्भे हरिपतिः॥५२॥  
गिरिगह्वरेषु गुरुगर्वगुम्फितो  
गजराजपोत न कदापि सञ्चरेः।  
यदि बुध्यते हरिशिशुः स्तनन्धयो  
भविता करेणुपरिशेषिता मही॥५३॥  
निसर्गादारामे तरुकुलसमारोपसुकृती  
कृती मालाकारो बकुलमपि कुत्राऽपि निदधे।  
इदं को जानीते यदयमिह कोणान्तरगतो  
जगज्जालं कर्ता कुसुमभरसौरभ्यभरितम्॥५४॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725196591Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

(५२) स्थितिं नो दध्या वासं मा कुरु। जटिलायां निम्नोन्नतायाम्। कुम्भिभ्रान्त्या गजोसाविति मत्वा। खरनखरैस्तीक्ष्णनखैर्विद्रावितो विदारितो महागुरुग्रावग्रामोत्यन्तगुरुशिलापुञ्जो येन तथाविधः। यः करिबुद्ध्या शिलापुञ्जमपि विदारयति सत्वां विदारयेदिति निश्चय एवेति भावः।

(५३) गुम्फितो वेष्टितः। पूरित इति यावत्। पोतः शिशुः। स्तनन्धयः स्तनपायी। भविता भविष्यति। करेणुः करिणी। हारीशेशुः सर्वानेव करिणो हनिष्यति। केवलं करिण्य एवावध्यत्वादवशिष्टा भविष्यन्तीति भावः।

(५४) कर्ता करिष्यति। अस्मिन् मालाकारस्येतरवृक्षसाधारणी बुद्धिरनुचितैवेति भावः।

**यस्मिन् वेल्लति सर्वतः परिचलत्कल्लोलकोलाहलै  
र्मन्थाद्रिभ्रमणभ्रमं हृदि हरिद्दन्तावलाः पेदिरे।  
सोऽयं तुङ्गतिमिङ्गिलाङ्गकवलीकारक्रियाकोविदः  
कोडे क्रीडतु कस्य केलिकलहत्यक्तार्णवो राघवः॥५५॥  
लूनं मत्तगजैः कियत् कियदपि छिन्नं तुषारार्दितैः  
शिष्टं ग्रीष्मजभीष्मभानुकिरणैर्भस्मीकृतं काननम्।  
एषा कोणगता मुहुः परिमलैरामोदयन्ती दिशो  
हा कष्टं ललिता लवङ्गलतिका दावाग्निना दह्यते॥५६॥  
स्वर्लोकस्य शिखामणिः सुरतरुग्रामस्य धामाद्भुतं  
पौलोमीपुरुहूतयोः परिणतिः पुण्यावलीनामसि।  
सत्यं नन्दन किं त्विदं सहृदयैर्नित्यं विधिः प्रार्थ्यते  
त्वत्तः खाण्डवरङ्गताण्डवनटो दूरेऽस्तु वैश्वानरः॥५७॥  
स्वस्वव्यापृतिमग्नमानसतया मत्तो निवृत्ते जने  
चञ्चूकोटिविपाटितारस्फुटो यास्याम्यहं पञ्जरात्।  
एवं कीरवरे मनोरथमयं पीयूषमास्वादय–  
त्यन्तः सम्प्रविवेश वारणकराकारः फणिग्रामणीः॥५८॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725196975Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

(५५) वेल्लति चलति। कल्लोलो महानूर्मिः। हरिद्दन्तावला दिग्गजाः। तिमिङ्गिलो मत्स्यभेदः। कवलीकारो गिलनम्। राघवो मत्स्यभेदः। द्वितीयार्धेऽनुप्रासः स्पष्ट एव।

(५६) लूनं खण्डितं तुषारार्दितैर्हिमपीडाभिः।

(५७) पुरुहूत इन्द्रः। सहृदयैर्विधिरिदं प्रार्थ्यत इत्यन्वयः। खाण्डवं कुरुक्षेत्रगतो वनविशेषः। अर्जुनेन खाण्डववनसमर्पणेन वह्निस्तर्पित इति प्रसिद्धमेव।

(५८) मत्तो निवृत्ते मद्विषयचित्तवृत्तिमकुर्वाणे। अररपुटं कपाटपुटम्। अन्तः पञ्जरमध्ये। वारणकराकारः करिशुण्डादण्डसदृशः। फणिग्रामणीः

**रे चाञ्चल्यजुषो मृगाः श्रितनगाः कल्लोलमालाकुला–  
मेतामम्बुधिकामिनीं व्यवसिताः सङ्गाहितुं वा कथम्।  
अत्रैवोच्छलदम्बुनिर्भरमहावर्त्तैः समावर्तितो  
यद् ग्रावेव रसातलं पुनरसौ यातो गजग्रामणीः॥५९॥  
पिब स्तन्यं पोत त्वमिह मददन्तावलधिया  
दृगन्तानाधत्से किमिति हरिदन्तेषु परुषान्।  
त्रयाणां लोकानामपि हृदयतापं परिहर–  
न्नयं धीरं धीरं ध्वनति नवनीलो जलधरः॥६०॥  
धीरध्वनिभिरलं ते नीरद मे मासिको गर्भः।  
उन्मदवारणबुद्ध्या मध्येजठरं समुच्छलति॥६१॥  
वेतण्डगण्डकण्डूति–पाण्डित्यपरिपन्थिना।  
हरिणा हरिणालीषु कथ्यतां कः पराक्रमः॥६२॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725207032Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

सर्पश्रेष्ठः। अत्र विषादनालङ्कारोऽप्रस्तुतप्रशंसाघटकतया स्थितः। विषादनं चाभीष्टार्थविरुद्धलाभः।  
(५९) चाञ्चल्यजुषश्चञ्चलाः। कल्लोला महान्तस्तरङ्गाः। अम्बुधिकामिनीं नदीम्। व्यवसिता उद्युक्ताः। वात्रावधारणे प्रश्नदृढीकरणे वा। उच्छलन्नुद्गच्छन्नम्बुनिर्भरो येषां तथाविधैर्महावर्तैर्महाम्भोभ्रमैः समावर्तित इतस्ततश्चलितः। ग्रावा पाषाणः। गाहमानो गजो यत्र शं नालभत तत्र भवतां का कल्याणकथेति भावः।

(६०) स्तन्यं पयः। मददन्तावलधिया मत्तवारणभ्रमेण।

(६१) नीरद मेघ। उन्मदो मत्तः। मध्येजठरं जठरस्य मध्ये। पारे मध्ये षष्ठ्या वेत्यव्ययीभावः। प्राचीनानां मतेऽसम्बन्धेपि सम्बन्धरूपेयमतिशयोक्तिः। स च सम्बन्धो वर्ण्योत्कर्षार्थः। यथास्मिन् पद्ये सिंहीवचने समुच्छलनासम्बन्धेपि समुच्छलनसम्बन्धोक्तिः शौर्यातिशायिका। नव्यास्तु नेमामतिशयोक्तिं मन्यन्ते।

(६२) वेतण्डो गजः। परिपन्थी विरोधी। अस्य तात्पर्यार्थः (५१) पद्यस्येव।

**नीरान्निर्मलतो जनिर्मधुरता वामामुखस्पर्धिनी  
वासो यस्य हरेः करे परिमलो गीर्वाणचेतोहरः।  
सर्वस्वं तदहो महाकविगिरां कामस्य चाम्भोरुह  
त्वं चेत् प्रीतिमुरीकरोषि मधुपे तत्त्वां किमाचक्ष्महे॥६३॥  
लीलामुकुलितनयनं किं सुखशयनं समातनुषे।  
परिणामविषमहरिणा करिनायक वर्धते वैरम्॥६४॥  
विदुषां वदनाद्वाचः सहसा यान्ति नो बहिः।  
याताश्चेन्न पराञ्चन्ति द्विरदानां रदा इव॥६५॥  
औदार्यं भुवनत्रयेऽपि विदितं सम्भूतिरम्भोनिधे  
र्वासो नन्दनकानने परिमलो गीर्वाणचेतोहरः।  
एवं दातृगुरोर्गुणाः सुरतरोः सर्वेऽपि लोकोत्तराः  
स्यादर्थिप्रवरार्थितार्पणविधावेको विवेको यदि॥६६॥  
एको विश्वसतां हराम्यपघृणः प्राणानहं प्राणिना-  
मित्येवं परिचिन्त्य मास्म मनसि व्याधानुतापं कृथाः।**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725207479Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

(६३) वामा ललना। महाकविगिरां कामस्य च सर्वस्वमित्यन्वयः। कवयस्त्वां वारंवारमुपमानतयाङ्गीकुर्वन्ति कामस्य च त्वममोघमस्त्रमिति भावः। तदहो इत्युत्तरवाक्येनान्वीयते। यद्वा। तत् प्रसिद्धम्। मधुपे भ्रमरे। मद्यप इति च ध्वन्यते। आचक्ष्महे वयं तटस्था इति शेषः।

(६४) लीलामुकुलितनयनमिति क्रियाविशेषणम्। समातनुषे करोषि। परिणामे विषमो दुःसहः।

(६५) सहसाऽविमृश्य। पराञ्चन्ति परावर्तन्ते।

(६६) अर्थिप्रवराणां यदर्थितं याचितं तस्यार्पणविधौ। अविवेकेन सर्वेप्यन्ये गुणास्तथा न शोभन्त इति भावः।

(६७) अपवृणो निर्दयः। गूढाशया गुप्ताभिप्रायाः। त्वत्तुल्यकक्षास्त्वत्समानावस्थाः।

**भूपानां भवनेषु किं च विमलक्षेत्रेषु गूढाशयाः  
साधूनामरयो वसन्ति कति न त्वत्तुल्यकक्षाः खलाः॥६७॥  
विश्वास्य मधुरवचनैः साधून् ये वञ्चयन्ति नम्रतमाः।  
तानपि दधासि मातः काश्यपियातस्तवापिच विवेकः॥६८॥  
अन्या जगद्धितमयी मनसः प्रवृत्ति  
रन्यैव काऽपि रचना वचनावलीनाम्।  
लोकोत्तरा च कृतिराकृतिरार्यहृद्या  
विद्यावतां सकलमेव गिरां दवीयः॥६९॥  
आपद्गतः किल महाशयचक्रवर्ती  
विस्तारयत्यकृतपूर्वमुदारभावम्।  
कालागुरुर्दहनमध्यगतः समन्ता-  
ल्लोकोत्तरं परिमलं प्रकटीकरोति॥७०॥  
विश्वाभिरामगुणगौरवगुम्फितानां  
रोषोऽपि निर्मलधियां रमणीय एव।  
लोकम्पृणैः परिमलैः परिपूरितस्य  
काश्मीरजस्य कटुताऽपि नितान्तरम्या॥७१॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725208021Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

अत्रौपम्यप्रदर्शनस्य व्याधानुतापनाशः फलम्।

(६८) काश्यपि पृथ्वि। क्षोणिर्ज्या काश्यपी क्षितिरित्यमरः।

(६९) अन्या लोकोत्तरा। गिरां वाचां दवीयो दूरतरम्। अवर्णनीयमित्यर्थः। अतिशयोक्तिरियं प्राचीनानां मते। अतिशयश्चात्राभेदेपि भेदो लोकोत्तरत्वप्रतिपत्त्यर्थः। अस्मिन् पद्ये प्रवृत्त्यादीनामन्यत्वं वर्ण्यमानं लोकोत्तरत्वं प्रतिपादयति।

(७०) महाशयानामुदारप्रकृतीनां चक्रवर्ती श्रेष्ठः। कालागुरुः कृष्णचन्दनः। इयं प्रतिवस्तपमा।

(७१) लोकम्प्टणैर्लोकतर्पकैः। काश्मीरजस्य कुङ्कुम्मस्य। इयमपि प्रतिवस्तूपमा।

**लीलालुण्ठितशारदापुरमहासम्पद्भराणां पुरो  
विद्यासद्मविनिर्गलत्कणमुषो वल्गन्ति चेत् पामराः।  
अद्यश्वः फणिनां शकुन्तशिशवो दन्तावलानां शशाः  
सिंहानां च सुखेन मूर्धसु पदं धास्यन्ति शालावृकाः॥७२॥  
गीर्भिर्गुरूणां परुषाक्षराभि-  
स्तिरस्कृता यान्ति नरा महत्त्वम्।  
अलब्धशाणोत्कषणा नृपाणां  
न जातु मौलौ मणयो वसन्ति॥७३॥  
वहति विषधरान् पटीरजन्मा  
शिरसि मसीपटलं दधाति दीपः।  
विधुरपि भजतेतरां कलङ्कं  
पिशुनजनं खलु बिभ्रति क्षितीन्द्राः॥७४॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725208701Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

(७२) लीलया लुण्ठितः शारदापुरमहासम्पद्भपरो यैस्तेषाम्। महापण्डितानामित्यर्थः। लीलालुण्ठितशारदापुरधियामस्मादृशानां पुर इति रसगङ्गाधरे पाठः। तेनायं श्लोकः कविनात्मानमुद्दिश्य रचित इति भाति। विद्यासद्मनो विनिर्गलन्तो ये कणास्तान् मुष्णन्त्यपहरन्ति तथाविधाः। अल्पविद्या इत्यर्थः। वल्गन्ति कत्त्थन्ते। पामरा मूर्खाः। अद्यश्वोऽद्य वा श्वो वा। सुप्सुपेतिसमासः। समनन्तरमेवेत्यर्थः। शालावृकाः श्वानः। शालावृकाः कपिक्रोष्टुश्वान इत्यमरः। अर्थापत्त्यलङ्कारोऽयम्। अर्थापत्तिश्च केनचिदर्थेन तुल्यन्यायत्वादर्थान्तरस्यापत्तिः। महापण्डितानामग्रेऽल्पविद्या वल्गन्ति चेत् तुल्यन्यायत्वाच्छकुन्तपोताः फणिनां मूर्धसु पदं धास्यन्तीत्यप्यायातमेव।

(७३) शाणो रत्नपरिष्करणपाषाणः। जातु कदाचिदपि। वैधर्म्येणेयं प्रतिवस्तूपमा।

(७४) पटीरजन्मा चन्दनः। इयं मालाप्रतिवस्तूपमा। अत्र वहनाधानभजनभरणानां वस्तुत एकार्थतैव।

**सत्पूरुषः खलु हिताचरणैरमन्द-  
मानन्दयत्यखिललोकमनुक्त एव।  
आराधितः कथय केन करैरुदारै-  
रिन्दुर्विकासयति कैरविणीकुलानि॥७५॥  
कृतमपि महोपकारं पय इव पीत्वा निरातङ्कः।  
प्रत्युत हन्तुं यतते काकोदरसोदरः खलो जगति॥७६॥  
पाण्डित्यं परिहृत्य यस्य हि कृते बन्दित्वमालम्बितं  
दुष्प्रापं मनसाऽपि यो गुरुतरैः क्लैशैः पदं प्रापितः।  
रूढस्तत्र स चेन्निगीर्य सकलां पूर्वोपकारावलिं  
दुष्टः प्रत्यवतिष्ठते तदधुना कस्मै किमाचक्ष्महे॥७७॥  
खलः कापट्यदोषेण दूरेणैव विसृज्यते।  
अपायशङ्किभिर्लोकैर्विषेणाशीविषो यथा॥७८॥**

<MISSING_FIG href="../books_images/U-IMG-1725209846Screenshot2024-08-25225205.png"/>

(७५) अनुक्तोऽप्रार्थितः। स्वयमेवेत्यर्थः। उदारैर्महद्भिः। कैरविणी कुमुदिनी। अयं दृष्टान्तालङ्कारः।

(७६) निरातङ्को निःशङ्कः। काकोदरः सर्पः। सोदरः सहोदरः। सदृश इत्यर्थः। यथा सर्पः पयः पीत्वा दातारमेव दशति तथा खलोऽपि महोपकारं विस्मृत्योपकारिणं हन्तुं यतत इति भावः।

(७७) पाण्डित्यं परिहृत्य सदसद्विवेचनशक्तिरूपं विद्वत्त्वं त्यक्त्वा। बन्दित्वमालम्बितं स्तुतिपाठकत्वं स्वीकृतम्। यस्य हिताय सत्यासत्यमविगणय्य मिथ्यास्तुतिः कृतेति भावः। हिरत्र निश्चये विषादे वा। रूढः प्राप्तपदतया बद्धमूलः। प्रत्यवतिष्ठते परिपन्थी भवति। दृष्टेषु कृत उपकारः परिणामे न सुखं जनयतीति तात्पर्यार्थः।
